MediaMind, 24/7 Deal


On ClickZ, Susan Kuchinskas reports that WPP's 24/7 and MediaMind have inked a new partnership which could mean convergence is ever-closer as data-driven, addressable media comes to TV. Kuchinskas quotes DG MediaMind SVP Andrew Bloom who "said that MediaMind and 24/7 have been working on deeper integration to allow joint customers within WPP using MediaMind to more easily access the audience insight and buying capabilities of ZAP (Zeus Audience Platform). (...) Next, the two companies will work on dynamic creative optimization, allowing MediaMind's Smart Versioning product that lets advertisers optimize creative based on audience information access ZAP's audience data." A particularly good deal for MediaMind - a holding company "blessing". WPP, meanwhile, looks for solid options other than Google. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012RD2N8BZBkX3segcfzen3yTuINWUzWJID67c2zdmiAuqi8gAqxjYn5XhQlk2Rm4dM5MMr445zgF0cHXX5OT9zQKc_ikVerbJ8OV3CUVbgt3fipA82Wj0oukWItUKeXaQfnQCdU45GM1E0uQ2lE8PEiWw8ykE2F73ul32uC1E6jeq9yH23Nzc5ytuaz2Axq0kNxSPELy4xJc=> . And, read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012RD2N8BZBkU5ksT_4nmCn1Lcmr-g7i2CrrC2lOYu3LylG4_mGD_R6uwey3tFgAgAesoI29_dNcm5Y81-xvGS64GFVeaMnRHiOtnKa9kvA267twZ2zNoYN26EGK4thIiSoCJZktlK16elRc6dBJ3rXIHIB8H_s0pXCaV3Iv4l7RfEjOPp6Phlnw==>

Del Rey writes, "Mr. Hecht said he envisions great opportunity for the brand to build out its offerings in mobile, where it has already experienced success, as well as multiscreen experiences. He also wants to improve the channel's international presence, especially in Europe." Natural Born Clickers Redux


What is it about Saturday that makes people click on ads more on Facebook? That's what new data shows from TBG Digital. Brittany Darwell explains to the unitiated on the Inside Facebook blog, "Facebook ad clickthrough rate is closely tied to cost per click and cost per impression. Ads with higher CTR are generally served more frequently. When ads have lower CTR, advertisers typically have to increase their bid price to get the same number of impressions. Facebook advertisers who want to maximize the CTR of their ads might decide to shift campaigns to the weekend when the averages seem to be in their favor." The "lean back" of the weekend appears to create more clicks, more engagement in a social environment. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012RD2N8BZBkXtdNK6jHlY-Id1r5fG659oyEv5JYABEtuIXi1PUdtGfeEdEX76hDuA9wLFdnbJu2yX9z1AB_RAvI-_qk89pYRaPr29cevg08v7cVM-HLgL5K4Utmup0Y1yikZ2iAD6UYNxGRH8V9SqZIOWqOa07YPsaRvYRsFbaxnGnvBxc3w5R8xFuxXNEkBgk3w5in3hEn02fmZW0RsfwcfNz-12BmoJKQHwkNIarn8=>  


Digital In China


The Boston Consulting Group has release a new report on the growth of digital media in China. Lots of interesting stats and prognostication. "In 2011, Chinese consumers spent 1.9 billion hours a day online-an increase of 60 percent from two years earlier. This surge was powered by both an expanding Internet user base and a greater online presence. The average time online per person increased from 2.8 to 3.6 hours per day between 2008 and 2011. Chinese users average about an hour a day more online than U.S. Internet users. Television viewing, meanwhile, declined from 1.7 to 1.4 hours during those years." Read it (sign-up required) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012RD2N8BZBkUWXlmyH1z4LiVnhV4T2Juk1b2O-IipYdDj9APqGltpUXQGqqtqUGZF5lXbMlmp3V3RtoEix_4J1iu7_zkiA-IhH3nfNAENSgzsLIMSMKZL3seSW1feB8AWEPph5UcOD_hjLwCzfAajne4NJCULdaWU1v7pdbRzNxKdPGbiDBoLNSeSkTJPZZ4KciqGP5_in0VqvNBdCkw6PbbzMuzVbjkDldCMXhhqA80=> .

In-Store Ad Network


Digital-out-of-home ad network for your mobile phone? PointInside calls it a private mobile ad network - nSide - and it rides inside a retailer app - another, potential "showrooming" weapon for offline retailers. GigaOm's Ryan Kim explains <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I1ESpFuCSgDgZA2PK4akCHFc1d5Yb47bY3j8xtfrV7qD3Co0-lNjCHFDRDUd4nhZJMngzRODfw0wpd6o6ki9QDiqDArv3WpV6w43U8-JU5cF58waO7lmsqfv09RaFN57G8uCXN86GikSu2pVjB9xT4AdlXhfy_und7kjKmC6p9ZE6eNNiw6D24QS26cMALgAfk=> , nSide technology enables "users to create shopping lists, see specials and find items in the store. When a customer goes to the actual store nSide takes their browsing patterns, shopping list items, and purchase history if available and matches it with their exact location and expected path inside a store to offer up relevant deals or coupons from the retailer and its brand partners." Seems like Foursquare could be a player here, too. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I0Ld6TZ7qud2iuR-gKckCsOcrb0A6ZWVkUrA8Llhf2tmH3xz5afrY56d0b4nFp5v27qoZ_m21y7BohHH6ViUq6NeZuh8aDGnCaia1k2oQEkCYD0XXRzpWWZWEUjhxR1_VU9LgLdTIInkTsGzDo_WyuU> . 


Pass The Real-Time


The Washington Post has begun running its real-time ad campaigns using its own home-grown technology. TechCrunch's Anthony Ha exhales, "The idea of real-time advertising is hardly a new one, but as The Post noted, they're usually offered by ad tech companies or ad networks." Geo-targeted for the Washington area, the real-time part here appears to be the social feeds which are pulled into the ads in real-time. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I2uLyWcyGDnWbAwneJVmxvJFLgUzWxo4YTnkUL8se9r2JoxJlpvo5BGDpwLn2436oIxBbsQcnsLyEfzCBMoz1qPuIF1LWiMf0yS3QnmNpyeboYSSm_FkXNRjVbhS8Lwlj8AkCDjCoFF1JiJSq7jKjx2DT-JRNWtBSJ-QBhMpxk3hw==>  


Targeting Event Audiences


On The Scout Research blog, the publisher analytics firm's SVP of Strategy, Matt Shanahan, pivots off of some B2B media spend data from Veronis Suhler Stevenson and paints a careful analysis on the interplay of the event and display advertising businesses. He concludes, in part, "Events have more fixed costs and revenue risks compared to digital display advertising. Consequently, sizing and locating the events to correctly match the audience is critical. Over time, the publisher can begin to benchmark the specific conversion rates of different events with the audience, and model even more closely to the revenue potential." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I1rc4qkt2vSAr4lJxZu9_3_2dzzgCIEGazFw7w8fnRe3o82oHiIcii542SGrSv0dsqSIZEBBkfWlaLQr5wtXIynK6Rqf7ELa1DMduLhqQuN5QVR2Fo7V8L-3alBSuNZad0RcENawtDwJp7JPASXVmhE-3Tnw4Zphgn7VbT8i7GY-VuXMVKoKOh-U2--ZcPDM50gNoaiZKRrU8O3FL1yp_GLErcLF4HzCmLg79getpyxhA==> . 


Let's Plan


BrightRoll Exchange follows its announcement last week that its video ad inventory would be open for bidding through AppNexus with new tools looking to serve planners. The company says in a release, "Inventory Planner, VideoRank and BrandWatch are proprietary tools integrated into the company's exchange (BRX) that enable buyers to streamline the planning, performance and safety of digital video campaigns." Read more about the tools <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I0YTEWpXK_6wAJ_bg64jMAoyy99fsFgsG0MXkk6dFufe5hL5-9qMn3b1uJuRyKpSHNoZ3HDGGFzMy84tnvKOUHWtkqwZUa3xYLWqydC98DtP_B9IhrVHtvhaY_Ow3VObwZ_74uwBwHUs8xIRPst1Fsk9m8YAnjqe8wYj5pkmZR1k0ucoVslBZD1sqTCBavDQE20yYll2ycPfQiGWW7GrXAuvWM5SnsP3RO622zyklpiv3JsHt6RQ7-r7wixwOWv-Q4=> .

Read more (but you will need to know Chinese) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I28YIoBLjTNllq1kQeiU8aNEbOInIuT4CKQ8px6SR3gH09cvnD94WtojoC5Z1IV1U81Mf7q3bprRUF21ij6UhPlM55hCSKI66lJtB2QEomhvKG-NL1BpN_k53ldshxf5ZArIdIZdC3vCMGJIQhTzSBpGGeqPmXbvUB5H6SWKsbsjNj805ZcYLaZ> . The B2B Social Ad Network


LinkedIn is quietly building new features into its platform which echo the targeting on B2C site Facebook. According to MediaPost's Mark Walsh, "LinkedIn just introduced a service that allows businesses to tailor content sent to followers according to various criteria, including industry, seniority, job function, company size, non-company employees and geography. Those are among the same targeting categories available to third-party advertisers on LinkedIn through its self-serve ad solution." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I2RjcX5wWcniebObOhkwd0pI0YZ_SGaUZ8SbSzd3RZudMOABKzLgLncAWQoB7rGpUffvEZyg00jXccy-ta9vFZCqee_hbUH4T5r9A725pffUHNFLd9ohwmNfwtb3W7OP4xDBbERi1yXxIq3r3PKFbRaGMkDmLX0JjM6uoOZf36k2snBFoz1Qh6WvGPAnDoLFq93rpNl1dbFR7S1qCy1vbg3Dvm_ZSihdbLRtWjIOQI4PQ==> . 


Showroom Harakiri


Showrooming is under the microscope again at The Wall Street Journal as, ironically, brick and mortar retailers are being underpriced by their online doppleganger. The WSJ's Ann Zimmerman finds that a new study by the investment research arm of William Blair shows, "Big retailers often have better prices online than in their stores; Target.com's are 2% cheaper than those in its stores and Wal-Mart's are 1% less, the William Blair study found." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xvwa90Sf8I0WWOdy53LHn1LGd5QLHI_PbyDGlV60WY9cmxQ6BoszWmKgluQ8HcLLFhoopOY-dcqe2XM2slY4UNoZgNUQvb0zhLu_x0hnIh4YHOowGZl7WpyvN4UFiMeffQfzqwhSygCIuRi-mdTxhsRYOVxhEPtXQ4Mt7buMlMkRfcxboZmldRpHVckVcArq> .

Yahoo! Re-Org


On All Things D, Kara Swisher shares a new memo sent by Yahoo! CEO Scott Thompson to Yahoos worldwide. The company's being grouped into three silos - Consumer, Regions and Technology. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZEnjGTw2Ako8tXnGTM2A2z8oz1l0lgIhB2G5sYdG9SkMaAzzIOT3n7cXEhoSOSP4QHCHCX3iEOI8Ca-Pd96WATz0_bO7wjxDrJbsw1HmyZcVW1fAxnOCp3oU93VmJtfv1UJIWcQg3VS0vee5a9g6mJk1kxNsnA0_MkFIp5-4Pa2G9ix2m6KT0io_11es9sBt-WrqlXxEDW_jmGeBIjSRJA==> . Even Right Media Exchange makes an appearance in the "Tech" silo of the memo: "Core Platforms, led by Mark Morrissey (LinkedIn) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZEnjGTw2AkqlMGTpCZt2Oug5m4qxB_bg-38PpSY8MN8lcOJIsst7Fd_kB43-V6tsvG3d4yRncriCv3LniOW5sgP7NAv3mgNkvr0FAJH51ioeIsWyvfZMizp3lmOynrtYUrNoqyc9b8kWOKuOrbbYYZNZdbCSZGMb> , will provide the foundational platforms, technology, and research to enable great customer products and leverage Yahoo!'s vast data stores to enable deep personalization and optimized monetization. Mark's teams will lead Apt, RMX, User Data & Analytics, our content optimization relevance engine (CORE), Yahoo! Labs and other key technology functions." Morrissey led the problematic search deal with Microsoft and architected Apt. Will he pour engineering fuel into it? Ad Age's Jason Del Rey smells a possible sale of RMX <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZEnjGTw2AkowRFpqy39i0Y6RSbNfKyactlwohVJF6bizCu8e_JZm5UACczh37GRyYI4i9XrH8j1tehwlfP3uHHXydfkPC79z6Xk_YqH0U-6S5tT3aWGZhYEre3OUDDnEjehSEB7z4rZq6bgPVQEVW7-ZqSNlYrjibPZ-nIxHi9VkmApVRmae6j-0gZcMWmZa> . Also of note, former Chief Product Officer Blake Irving is no longer with the company. After reviewing the memo, a source close to Yahoo! tells AdExchanger that Yahoo has proven they can execute advertising solutions across their owned and operated properties and should continue to do so. But, challenges remain when providing solutions across the industry -and that perhaps it's time to focus on the Company rather than the industry. 


Video Viewability


Tremor Media is entering the viewable impression fray with its Video Hub technology as the company announced in a release "video ad verification signals that give advertisers insight into the viewability of their ads, including where they appear on the page, the size of the player, and the impact on the viewer experience. The new 'Player Position' and 'Player Size' signals are the first measurement features that offer advertisers and publishers full transparency into video ad position and size for video campaigns running across ad networks, direct publishers and video exchanges." Given momentum in display and even video, the viewability metric seems to be destined to become a key, universal metric in short order. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZEnjGTw2AkqYGDQt5l6gVtYtFNBt8VE3xp0OTKA2GJO1-28tdmxPIOonXElCYJ2hJEdFchGApCJqZLjN5CF3BXqyY3Mv6YaRLXo-IFb47yxGJEHxoXkKteSpBO-4xNRKG2SFGt-ETEHFTXL5p79tc2y_6hwi8lmH> . The overall goal is to improve an understanding of engagement with ads by the user on behalf of the marketer - and all of that presumably makes the marketer's ad spend more efficient. To my knowledge on the ad verification side, and industry-wide, there remains no automated contextual or semantic scan of video content other than what's on the page around the video. That remains a tough one. 


Rising Video


The IAB is bringing its successful Rising Stars competition to video advertising. Randall Rothenberg, President and CEO of the IAB says boldly in a release, "With these new formats, we will be creating advertising experiences in digital video that are as good or better than traditional broadcast." This echoes the convergence theme of the recent IAB Annual Leadership Meeting where NBCU's Peter Naylor was given the reigns as the IAB's new Chairman. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZEnjGTw2AkqvV7sErX_-iy58_qcHE6DbDEdNhKq1AlF6LDDcemTXQCNBsXqlGx03bCWmUEPfcSRiyJpryrTntP3s5lJjLG2-grp3kzN3kKM37Molj3B5VSIHcU6x2UutNEs2ud4CIRQQE6ChAh7WKFUuIJMMrVS6lcDyNiasIZmH2rav2WA1eC7cgcVkXXbTkyTjc5meBV4rXkDAo_GekB1Tio1-hXthyYwo0fBvay3PVB95cgT7kQ==>  And, enter the competition with your VAST or VPAID-compliant entry <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZEnjGTw2AkpCGcT9YpMdEB95jg4F2QfmgKvjCUzFkeSUj_zKL_iLnIrWpkBXtELvX7V8HuffjqTqFZTN1_MJppTfr5hD-wgWgR73em1pV0U8PhRHnPDpaYpictA9IyVfVvlD16f5wzw=> . And speaking of video standards, the IAB has updated them and now include a skippable ad format among other features. That number would represent around 19 percent of overall ad spending, said GroupM." About Q1


It may have been acquired, but Adobe's Efficient Frontier continues to publish its ad reports. This one covers Q1 and according to company data DoubleClick Ad Exchange continues to "capture market share" from Yahoo!'s Right Media Exchange. Also, the report takes up Google's CPC issues and finds, "Google search algorithmic changes contribute to growth in search spend: Increases in search spend are a result of increased click volume rather than increased CPC rates. This has been true for the past two quarters, but is contradictory to trends in prior quarters. Algorithmic changes to Google in Q4 2011, such as increased site links, have led to a greater proportion of branded traffic that does not impact CPC rates." More clicks, means users are more engaged with Google search, which means Google gets more data, which means Google gets smarter. Smart. GOOG Prognostications


Citi's Mark Mahaney is thinking about Thursday's Google Q1 earnings call in a note to investors. Mahaney talks about the decrease seen in CPCs for Google in Q4 - will it carry over???...."Should All Eyez Be On the CPC Prize? -- We believe investors will be heavily focused on CPCs, which declined 8% Y/Y in Q4 -- the first decline since the '08 Recession -- due to improved Ads Quality changes and the Mobile Monetization transition. We expect Q1 CPCs to be down a similar level. But we don't view the drivers as negative structural factors. And we believe total Search spend (which also incorporates Paid Clicks) a much better measure." It will also be interesting to see if Google breaks out its display revenues a bit more - maybe tell us something more about the Exchange's success, GDN direct, or owned-and-operated display. C'mon Google.. gimme some stats.

$1 Billion In Cash


"Hey look at you, Aol. Flush with $1 billion in cash... Gonna buy something?" Yesterday, Aol's cash balance just got a whole lot fatter (and so did the company's stock <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IVxasPaQe_z95X3j01lp56y_j1IWu4lPZKScEBQh-X7yDk-RtmzeP4Hm_HpbLfzqEkxPjb0Blxgu7RR2WgtAMc3YmXdJJWIdDThJK5v2Sg9CLSGkkZsQhk1KzLgBwQwYZNHXjXbhih3AA==> ) as Aol announced the sale of "800 patents related to advertising, search, e-commerce and mobile," according to Reuters which says Amazon, eBay, Google and Facebook were involved in the auction process. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IUaFe2-Zx714SFHkQotW-wYdsgEJ-jOFHDYKahHeYoPQTCT46dnz7-EWkTT0mxqjXzqdRFODCVwkhhXb03Oe4Dpp1kFE1XHCldcmly-2vRmoM2FHIs17zBdpgK_PIoODrWkWG61A4-X6pWr-5xsKPIjeDLBWJRggqEx4nmW_o5mzclZoDetXZA9lZk0WAPxrdA=> . And, read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IWqbeioIjNuXS9rTGPjFmIoV8z3ib6_JXa125zdD8WmNDH4wEa-sqx5Etjjlxjz-eeSPdOPkkcgH7EbKG24aCiK9KzpVX4K-3-6aVWS21N97dFvhM9W7pnKhELb0kMuSON18Juwk0cYr-YvH0v9t-oLU_0308Vs2PwtqiQOmgIPpkL0WhjTgU4cxEzAuTXI5m4=> . On All Things D, Peter Kafka's sleuthing reveals that the patent sale to Microsoft included assets from a long forgotten purchase of Netscape. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IXfnYHb8WX4ur0jPNBX9OOeU48LTLFUUONB4UesrUHtdODjvNm4RpzsgLJVeckmldOkNkkb0nFIdh2msl-J2KkZqKFHjx6wB7stsViGo3K-bzVKTzKNl6b_8Q1fc0b_owry05C6HEW6fNEj0wHk0LnLRIMKz8KSSyfLqA4WDpvaj7Ckdzzj8IekdJbe510jXvIRD9hZ0FVP54qsA5fHeRD1XqGkbtSboJ5jrMISUgBPwg==>  


Ad Tech Check


Reflecting on its first year of existence, The Council for Accountable Advertising (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IWd5E1cGxDdazaOe4iwpqcjNuKdHmLjqyaFRn3NVsUbaZfZXn515OvcRgBu26cU0b5eojlNDDX7fqxTE6uucMl_BvHYf2YCKf2vQbv2Q9RMwntaJuSLRqeX_zjJglTkKWP2WP7w044-AxOkxI8Js40O-SnisHiQ9727GQSzuvM4AhrNEI4hC4i9szV3Dc22hrQ=> &A 2011) says that its members have enjoyed a year of success and points to acquisitions of TARGUSinfo by Neustar and Admeld by Google among others. Looking ahead, the Council's Stephen Messer says that milestones to be achieved include "Standardized data integration guidelines, Universal API, and Interoperability for marketers..." Read the blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IWmgxSrArfOhfFK306wmdemvMswst4Z2vSS1Pn-Wml7j9DN9XhN2Xy_XfSCOn7pswvaGYE89LTNUauI6z4iERTDTWt3Q_9SXAVnDUGuQlHj_9_dLVxvFS1hF4reFnera0t1vX3Q2LBCERda1PghfjbgiFjsBQHIo3kWfoVOYAdvkIEjD6zjIxwnQVAMnHticHuvu29eXt243Q==>  


More Patent Wars


With Millennial Media flush with its own buckets of cash after a successful Initial Public Offering, Augme Technologies has announced that it will sue Millennial for violating its patents. According to Augme's press release, "Augme is asserting three causes of action involving patent infringement related to Augme-owned United States Patent No. 7,783,721 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IWAlA_7GQlZ5FXCsf_eXEFDHJ3XYLZwM6fVljM1rFQdk4OCwSgfCt43aHN3W9tkKgSc7YkuAJaEIkj4LjTeEnt-04fhDtvz8dGgD2gnI8LoLp7VcPUEnfbyebXdF_zl7uJXVI6nvsdxKQxfbhNXKcME3rmdAYMzM0qUgCIx3uP9YGW8HTyBGJhN41dicuQl0InZzPQ0S13oSg9gixsBDDYw834CWADBEwqRX2hYdFw8jCxo2M0RLjiHHzgnkp1zp0x6Cm4vnm5Q-TeYP-2EILBhl2EFPuKl1yJsjwilCTTe4hfwSyZuUpw2gnelYAjRgSe4TGYHuVwgiRorRHKcobjVC1ylIPFj9qUg3FXscGiWXgHN9KJD7jk8FCs757HcAOtbtU241Em1tA==>  ("Method and Code Module for Adding Function to a Web Page"), United States Patent No. 7,269,636 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IX5UScF_qEGPn_OF-Uav9g9-okHNEEJ1zQuqa-sJgXV_JS1T1l4Z-liditlxlBQ1pO2g5BCM03BAW0DMjhTZKtWxxgHdVwdtSm3eBbJxz_3B3k4ZIeK2yPTBwlVowSL2POY-PnnkzP7lPlVPhk8OzhbSlSOsd5EifSewr7vxh48i_V1hI_aSmlEUGyfPirsdDMMhTW2wywdzsjOiZiAdxl7K7qaKmb2Bqob2-o5e_-wGtkjQPercGei4L_vUjytVVkyx-Vd9G6JHKGpNgD2nuL-jeG98rQ9oUxpdPnsavEPukq2PNtRJlYsuBEDnBa0XymGwA8puN-G_8UxP3mFPmTH8y0Vs6CC-q3zY2h4ALrqho4jYF3jkknwjVi5SbV8F3alRcZpBX624g==>  ("Method and Code Module For Adding Function to a Web Page") and United States Patent No. 6,594,691 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IVV3KIr6SIU7QdC9kK2tpDRwaC1gLqksvPKbstxM-7GnTpdFVC6khTSCedTE5CRBbhtCywpoOP5KV9h-dkLhu2b4b8qes6C5MLrA1F43slrmWgx91zEsT9C942C9jJdJc_PetB0VostPfhn0JDlg3o-_tFu4SblHI1Zdxvb1lOkw1kBfw4wlRUxb9JYZHM7xzDv5JeLLsKbulUotoAv0oqFx7f8fLNk5zhPb3azrVB5EKt6ulG-JKVi76p62m7yoChg2HjeDc1HFuDJHzYEmBTwl2_-8Sc3jGJX0cOVBxf9WeDHv6aIml31GJDO_I1Wgh54zLsUx7FpU02TBAJbYX7MtqfZCWTHb-nSnO3qLmbYMgPFMKxiwKBI55RSqZeusEPPVLSffzuLUA==>  ("Method and System for Adding Function to a Web Page")." CPC Google


Wall Street's obsession with Google's Cost-Per-Click decrease <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IU61YSQSmTV-0f-SFZRt6miA-Z7l_AdkUOkY7_pXfJ3pauCQ8FEwVyCPWNRoNaSDc81Cs_PaFjWNdWEQpa8SkXNOC_qbMQb9Qybb6MEERdMwSPCoTbRQyZ2Iq1kDCCHgiiKy5rUuegP9sADyV9wg80atqfXobpgm4E=>  last quarter is raised again by The Wall Street Journal in advance of Google's coming, Q1 2012 earnings release. Read it. (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IWPeoebCUXKLod2lZBU2ZkhYNWLLyzbdY5UL4g2oXrHkYoNRaQdeT1Wle3fYP0lyMFWTy80gXRNiOijiHeLwnHVIkITZVukH2CaGWUHnJyjXQ9HGuDJygzQDvfEYG4iTcWvR7wMHThEF3rCmaW78kdrQuh3pftWBO1SsChuYbYufNUarqoGUrk6>  The WSJ's John Letzing writes, "In January, Google executives said there had been a number of reasons for the decline in prices paid for clicks, noting that more clicks on Google ads is a good thing, even if it does lower prices for advertisers." 


RPC Pinterest


In an opinion piece on VentureBeat, Convertro CEO Jeff Zwilling says his company's attribution data is impressive revenue per click from social media darling Pinterest. He offers, "In Q2 2011 Pinterest.com represented 1.2% of social media revenue for e-commerce sites. It now represents 17.4% and is quickly gaining on Facebook. (That shift from 1.2% to 17.4% is based on measurements we made across 40 of our client sites - most of which are top 500 internet retailers.)" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IXd4FJBV4FdGfTVbeosx8Q-5CL22zJwg7GccVzxGRODyUOV8HWxGtx4HGJ-IRQPx7RPB1mEZIl5wWwUORyCOveFVS1HsRT-7uD_umxwt3UrH3Z_q8HJuLyqUprQPL9j94opQQrmzfhgE10qzeYwwRM6AcTLM6SZTagXs5hZmv7v3fe97oJl7yk48_Cz7htpOuNff0x6ckl70sJ8W7iLNXMJ>

Clickity, Click


On ClickZ, Adnetik COO Nathan Woodman unearths the comScore/Starcom study <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IXMwvv88V9xBJBMiPsh5G9aJ68vAAixpdpQ63c2RK66d0WK7rzgPwB9gfrmjPd6NNxpEvbdgvWlEnGqOawLdMhdefNhgz-9QYz5VwAori1i96aZSLfzJVnlnBlZQbuxjA-ZMFGwqhCBFM8kfA31APgJnLWFJ3YqSxfnh4j7jUdnw7zsh_WX9GLb-adappmRdZFT0aiSuQggarE_LnzSVsi0T757ecDH5kmqZHNiyqStbY6dUTnah_ygJxNQxfF9ZRZPDudU2aZ3giqmAQP9YEkT04uK9DY6GNE9r-aUEzu5prWpTe25zGeXPeJeFzRpz0cR2hOErz6UTgJKMR5fVyuHF_HWjaF17GxtIVSzxTBPaA==>  on "natural born" clickers and then reveals results from a recent study of his own. Woodman writes, "In a sample of 200,000 random clickers taken in March 2012, I found that 40 percent of the clicks were produced by 20 percent of the clickers. This data suggests there is substantial bias to a macro segment that can be described as frequent display ad clickers." The clicker audience! Read about it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IVXyrhSg50kOj-cj5YC_6jEA4S5QTYjCIzA4QEKKeIxQ9N8gtA7ZUuJSEIIk5KMTMkl3mxYuhBiPovJUV65ltOZqd6j_GjgzBxijBb8U6BKJvWgEWxWgv4wJvlxQlx_sbr8bGasmPAhUp6KGh5ZZj8MkbPiutjWSPYH54svYGWPZQ==>  


Digits Do The Walking


AT&T has less interest in the Yellow Pages than it used to as it was announced that a private equity firm would take 53% ownership in the Yellow Pages. The Los Angeles Times reports, "That leaves AT&T with 47% ownership of the new entity, which includes the YP.com website, the YP advertising network, a related mobile app as well as the hard-copy books." The entire entity is worth about $1.4 billion. Read more about an old school, end-to-end, offline-to-online solution <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001XAeYTfsY8IX59cBkapDfOR7gh07-kpsZfo5-0XnrGqy3hAE4hP1tLs9zoC7SR-GKR1PO5w69mJyKIxqB8r5hFR5FYIN85dN8boGq0F8hyx5RKdnwvL3cOiRkG22YxlFAMjoXuHmE0Ser8zQISVroA5ZDS_IuKYJWdidWFWy582hDNeKLbw4Y6fRgzyej6A7Vm14gf-hUaKRFB0ooX9iKwQ==> .

Evaluating Ad Tech


Sensing a need on the client and agency sides to crowdsource opinion on the latest digital tech, MediaPost's Laurie Sullivan covers the creation of the DMR Index (see the site) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMePyvVxr9NUq2Djc-bs_Fs8vI_Ff-Kp02K2JLFBoUQdhXWQ-4qOmPuC8yn2YYXkHGrAMyz9x9-l7D67kD17jZT4RMWoTa9rjbtYRF_NYZFvqCw==> , which Sullivan writes "will help to connect clients with the best vendors and solutions, as identified by advertisers' reviews and comments." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeOdKwxoNyeUaGhvuqsPHl4o-ZlGUQELZImrKFegQpy7O-IjOVqPUBUr17CnLAZUbR-Ff82mbHTlZNO_dorRn_cv1F5JPV-bS9FhN-ZJ9244AqsGUp1vTfPvdx70YKvlb0nr7i-lI7fV7CaiBwiu3fZqetk4tYTOmVuEMuc-oDqADxXyehZj-SOZTlh-ufAuIh20ML0z6U2zEjL30P5VvqU_X0u3MDthf24=>  Launched by DMR Partners leadership <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeMA7Z27iHWwfzm9IdPuVl4VeLwlQFhQaPpIlnOJxPq-GvDg0L0vuMWeLiPnXhtWZdY-viroA_uPMZJl9g5HTFXUqkslhPeWIsoCVtpxIK_OBLAz2WKDmauvz2Sdt4TQZaA=> , which includes former agency execs Sean Finnegan and Jessica Joines, former mobile and Adenyo exec Alec Andronikov, and former ValueClick-er Gayle Meyers, the site promises to subscribers "Search and review - from the hottest startups to established media tech platforms." Startups are urged to leave their company profile. "Reviews and rankings of companies are only available to view by agencies and brands," according to Sullivan. 


Private Exchange Machinations


In Ad Age, Jason Del Rey looks at display ad private exchanges and how publishers have come to terms with the new way of selling. He writes, "Forbes initially blacklisted advertisers that bought reserved inventory (in other words, prevented direct ad buyers from buying private exchange inventory), then reversed course. On the other hand, Condé Nast at first granted access only to advertisers that increased their direct-sales buys in fourth-quarter 2011 from the year before." As buyers AND sellers get a better idea what "first look" on inventory is worth, which is a key value prop of the private exchange, it would seem these private exchanges will evolve if not merge into the wider, "public" ad exchange. Might take a while though - it's still early days for the understanding and dissemination of all the data in a display ad auction. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeNPNNuRdoAzsh28-BSAH3bLxfTo4H2w2OF4FRa4Jt-1zBbvQIiKxIY6kJl4V9pCt_6ixuy55Wjq59dVvaURiO2du0TNWfJnbexE9BN7MFhO6VTTpqZakgTg3ywv_deBu2DIIS7vjvCEoRAnOYqTjNDPfiUPsQIaE1UGlKtyekayx_eiFwhSeYWwTV7dLGk2xbn25V5QqGsVtO8m4WXmtPtOEQiGF0U58f0=> . And, see Ad Age's new Audience Buying guide <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeNk1J1-1ooOqYkejOVNJv6yN8JqF04eWcd9awEcdw2k9h3IvRSAnMri4_x8pE1HSiArG3K7Odl7JaZeD2Kov1vHxODZknBNtXUH0DGyNVBQL2nmgCV2vRUA6CzUuWh1bpw=> .


Signal M&A


The social signal space got a little bit smaller last week as Visible Technologies bought Cymfony (both are WPP investments says Geekwire) for an undisclosed sum according to Geekwire. As you may recall, Salesforce.com bought social analytics and monitoring company Radian6 for over $300 million last year. For Visible, it means a new 125-person company and 200 total customers. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeMPp5_n_UKb5XuyOOfiPC6NA8dMG7KMkworrnL5gt871QBUMp-DBV89joyANkCxNS50IP-ng7JsixT_SNXx-8PHQK9DNSv95UGxj8l89o0A-HMrdlsYjink9V_7tJTVIYR2xEk6LEKjZE9xMijv_Qk-2kcNp4qeb-18XsfCQZBWOWrPSHtoPtBQJDNgl5cTOcpl5nmW8bQgfg_qPEoHb-3U>  


Examining Gamification


Increasingly, the gamification of ads has become a topic as pundits wonder whether making games out of ads really helps make them more relevant to the consumer. On his personal blog, Tom Fishburne writes, "More importantly, gamification can't make an un-engaging brand engaging. It may be the shiny new thing, but it's not a silver bullet. Game mechanics are enablers to big ideas. They aren't the big ideas themselves." Read - and see - more from the Marketoonist <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeO7-3rsC6geSNRdpi7Ngf4wAvgvMk2GuLEjIXqErRbPqyoSty5-vqEXXeVHh2OyUffPK7HhQpm5kHP10GvhDtAUz23SW_UZQS8ggjCLO69ITsQU9l40HPhOML_nbQwvkvmUwqKwNWxEvg==> . 


What They Know


The Wall Street Journal's "What They Know" series, which it looks at the use of consumer data by online technology and service companies, says that the business of Facebook apps is a treasure trove of personal data that users may not wish to have revealed. WSJ authors also write, "Dozens of apps allow advertisers that haven't been approved by Facebook within their apps, which enables advertisers including Google to track users of the apps, according to data collected by PrivacyChoice, which offers privacy services. Google said app-makers control which technology they use to deliver online ads." From here, though Facebook has never moved Google to the publicly approved list <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeNTBuULYvPbdzZ89h3fCVTdsapFmdH_mh3YzSqBkdjYKknsXkntEBPqkua-w4lMJRqf6SiWsfuKGH7uEbEAvszwNOF4oq7KeyymuY7pGYk2ZBZHBRbgykrWD8pNT5FudfUFKYTT6z20iw==>  (likely due to sticky, strategic considerations - read AdExchanger in April 2011 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeN8gc0oIIyD_Kb2DQd4qU2Stxkhbsi73qpHpSuhbUf-FAVa5kAHCBZz5_BPC5DgganvfVvqNXAhW_lCBOwXrYiAhr2CQZWqOHoMuZMYMlw4ZFUixgMKRSypGRGMVOKn5TMzOX--paiOdWfTuYRKpvhsrbxnNeifJuLgtkBz-cRYvr6T_L6Luc7Q> ), it has not stopped their use by app developers because Google AdSense and, by extension, the DoubleClick Ad Exchange, remain a key monetization mechanism for Facebook app developers. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeO7QMlkGlBJSpH9ztQQ1rvAGZ-KamykX1oFW69M1nAr87slIKfo01z2GCl-4Mqllgi0Pb49Rzeyo4qvuWCVZFXtPAzZfvy-nG4arHXl0DYccsoT4oxnJwlic1oKaCn1ZEFJWhCLRGqeHGF9SWY8ftAgTEGc1dKHVZu3z1Qy7AP9uoKKWABhWdEx> .

I, Invest - Agency-style


Joe Mandese reviews MDC Partners' kbs+p's burgeoning, venture investment efforts in an article on MediaPost. kbs+p venture maven Darren Herman tells Mandese that the agency-as-investor model has meant "the agencies have gained intellectual capital by learning the inner workings of new advertising technologies that could have a significant bearing on the ad industry, and by integrating key members of its agencies into those processes. On the flip side, he says the entrepreneurs involved in those startups have gained important insights into the advertising business that are likely to help with their success." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMePwaIZju9KUUKgat_00LkbbsoomPxo99k68RoM_PqtJ60AGnu0wFOmdl7fZrQ2qRAIZH4OhpXroZUSUxz6Kun99TQzxUDppnuo6VsCdcQfL8si1T-cgwun4hNwsvg-ZxzLs1mjTcbp3NRwvq8vaUF2wZbRx4wR6tcaJBVkG85xfp9aN0DZgfYBKLoZpl0fEGXDNQPp6O5o7Dm_9cT52-jbcYlIT7xq5UxJU61pZvrMAJV85l7ed049T> .


New Website


Rocket Fuel, which has gone by the moniker "ad network" for a while, has refreshed its website with a new design and without the phrase "ad network" according to a company rep. See it now! <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jS1SH-vJMeOXiJNJgaSlloIhYETSYBG-WAUTDISx0lScxSr9PuZtd3dLcdvyeE6yY7m16QWDyqswP8zjLy7Se-hpSTshqRSx1fB67Kte-syAKiencJA-fg==>  "Ad network" has had negative connotations in recent years, but the fact remains that a performance-driven solution using demand-side platform technology is essentially using the ad network model -whether it buys on a per-impression basis through networks and exchanges or direct-to-publisher. Arbitrage/margin can be the reward for performance and meeting the client's goals.

Huffington Ascending Aol


The New York Times' Brian Stetler says that Huffington Post growth is changing the strategy and direct report structure of the company as it looks to return to startup mentality according to Huff Po's Arianna Huffington. The Times's Stetler writes, "The revamping, she said, is intended to help The Huffington Post 'maintain the innovative spirit of a start-up.' Technology, business development, marketing and communications units that were woven into AOL last year will begin to report to her. The advertising sales unit will remain inside AOL 'at the moment,' she said." Huff Po is and was a data-driven ad business with heavy reliance on ad networks, exchanges, SSPs and so on in addition to custom/integrated sales. It will be interesting to see her "take" on ad tech strategy if she is let loose even further. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_n_dCOdSQoCm8MlVoGlhJefgGsk1_x2oG_HOZ-quCkltW3Vncnd8h643WdSqgQMQQMLfQkF_uMwiiFqtpb-2_uo10JdZSATzqtqSdykjt2hkzS7F-oofGX6Y7XpPsYqPeeESa4wemELTe10-dN5916vO68tqYnL3vRDye4FlGOUZjePaBQkNhh1oOpR9RgYeKI-mQXnR89FzchRnc7NoKA5fCbNXedxmuU=> . 


Scanning Euro Audience Buying


London-based trading desk Infectious Media has put together a "European RTB Insights Report." In a case study on what the company calls "borderless targeting", Infectious discusses how optimization played out with display bought via real-time bidding across countries. A sample using CPA goals from the company's own campaign data: "By day 8 all regions had begun to be optimised, with Scandinavia showing the strongest performance followed by the Mediterranean region, and then Germany and the Netherlands." Get it here (lower right of home page - pay with some PII, too.) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_kZeJlSo5INxrb87IDLVDRwGaITzGrL8aZNqL_BxJ5v4seOaoW-4LYqk8sOg_OXq2Mcrr85EG17UBwxfNPVg4KXcd_dviTFZ_0WBWKRHdY1xWnDcn8xFDmc> . 


Ad Network Legacy


RadiumOne CEO Gurbaksh Chahal takes the podium at Ad Age and weaves his company's belief in the importance of the social web to advertising. In particular, the former Blue Lithium CEO observes the evolution of the ad network: "So why will legacy ad networks die? Can't they just adapt? The analogy that comes to mind is the mechanic who attempts to fix a plane that's already in flight. Legacy ad networks have already taken off and, unfortunately for them, it is incredibly difficult to change their business model mid-flight to adapt to the demands of the Intelligent Web. They will need to develop entirely new products to exist in the Intelligent Web's highly social and real-time environment." Fly or die. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_nhfpaqcYRJH4vdFTTBs4nMxBtIdm9tAPHjhFcnAC_rghWlUvg1FjpfgWBTBPojPGaoCjGpLku4pKWP2KFbC4ZAoNdPX3tJ3lZpZoC4jInbRVuQsxyTE4KinN5CQXiFHJsh5BwofetMcCzlEBXkLH7tRWVPRlCpMSTZ4tUN-clbB93rGQhA9vsiaqAUPzh8qkk=>  


Updating Local Targeting


New enhancements to the Google Display Network are published on the Inside AdWords blog. Location-based targeting gets some re-working among other features: "Now, both the location extracted from the content of the page and the likely physical location can be used, making advanced location targeting applicable for the Display Network for the first time. The default setting is to show to people 'in' or 'viewing pages about' your targeted location, but you can edit this option at any time." There's also an update to a limited, search retargeting capability for location. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_mWsuRjqp8uo60LmFZ3r_VaNG7Onc1nlA_7abvK0jTbuXxHBH7HpVWym-duWHUQfQQoG5bT7aKtWPvqlQrR6vcVyNwCWQfEl_ctMcqYQ8qVTQpx0Ei6zE6CIXgeUzWlwF_QdD2U2v1A-UfcoQBEBd16JWBpj1pvIzKsuyFeAbx90kEL68v7_Y7C>  


Retargeting The Cart Owner


From the Shop.org blog, music for the ears of retargeter lovers as Shop.org's Fiona Swerdlow covers new research from SeeWhy on the eCommerce cart: "On average, 8% of customers return to a site to buy if the company does no remarketing. With a remarketing program in place, however, that average jumps to 26%. Yet - incredibly - just 37% of the retailers do 'something' as follow up to a customer visit (though usually something like asking customers to sign up for a newsletter). Only 12% did some cart remarketing of any kind, and even fewer truly personalized that follow up." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_n3TFoime161d7h9jggDGIHdAwC82TVtehVgrVaXVlDMHPdHPO1OayHmhTx9uh6mXUrVQh3idT4Y44uBBaEDVDC5jb9lZF31uvI6-nnkSOikMVA_b_sPniN4TzOtTpFIfzl9Dmz-0YuD8zEtoON_fOAh8knItUBlqs--Q06niqtslijZWcZmPInq5m_Nmf-0TI=>

An Agency Grows In Lagos


On Digiday, Jack Marshall pinpoints a trend among digital agencies to open up offices in countries considered irrelevant from an ad or marketing spend perspective. Matt Cronin of agency Web Liquid tells Marshall about his new Lagos, Nigeria office, "It's such an under-served market. Everyone looks at places like Brazil and China, but Nigeria is a great investment opportunity. It has a huge population, a growing economy, and their adoption of new technologies has been extremely fast. It has a huge population, a growing economy, and their adoption of new technologies has been extremely fast." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_kcj5hgQsQiL0HOCftkUWWPkqAt0IAYwGc_RTx8LcaRg0jsu8j4r8H9zCT8XIHJFclFqrdGXLsws5P49L_qKCaBcLc6CkvCgpttUza4H0xMoJxCTzSAYgtBAPrXCBPUGWZUeCKEjv37Rn_Nl4iquHu1JT6X-bAeagq1tF8KnjkbOw==>  


Tips For The Seller


On the Upstream Group blog, Doug Weaver delivers more sage tips to the seller crowd. Weaver writes, "I encourage every digital sales person to begin proactively negotiating the nature and measurement of campaign outcomes at the very earliest stages of the sales discussion. If you wait for the RFP (never a good idea, by the way) to tell you what's being measured and how, you're already screwed." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_lfa_V4ILR-81etArPzLMPKt8Qvc1dFBdY2Ciaq0zMqta6yOvmfa-KnuhB80joW7cWxPTsvmfQY5q7Ue8lOCnoKVgdg99pLrILXUbHMXE1maDxrqWraEvYZCZGUvHo444Ge3prxt1nljjDJ3NsOKmI8>  


I, Incubate


CPX has caught the incubation bug, too. At nearly the same time as yesterday's announcement of AppNexus Accelerate <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_kYgjxqPJP7iXiNG9TOHBgyVeX7_KkEl-XNoXGrTGMazgeE1ZHw33YAa6wOqZBMxfVC74zByzW-VahgMFkLqoO1g09EfAKCyvJi0Ve1VKLR4XzqZYpfdPJTTaTfFnYxkE6rpf6JlGnirRwihfPAYKGlpIn7FJNnkYrOhI3MY6LYnRkfKRQMn1LS56witENDqUJarJShSNFfUFsLErZcgdjd14p4vkyrH9swRpJG3LN-mg==>  startup incubator program, CPX Founder and CEO Mike Seiman said in a release, "Many brilliant entrepreneurs in need of initial funding and support don't require - or want - the involvement and oversight of typical VCs. If we can help by providing the limited capital and overhead they need and offering our unique expertise along the way, then we think there are significant synergies to explore." Read about the incubator's focus on yield. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_loYO8rEEq0A0jS9PSRjpDBlCnt5OvKp2vwXWxPAPGubLAVASlESlVmrADU4q8pe9_mfTXkbeLxGDZkaTMmsUfW0ljD5t_Uq0kkfVDexivTu1JDnloh7nniPvbe3SNQU_M=>  And, see more on CPX site <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_loYO8rEEq0A0jS9PSRjpDBlCnt5OvKp2vwXWxPAPGubLAVASlESlVmrADU4q8pe9_mfTXkbeLxGDZkaTMmsUfW0ljD5t_Uq0kkfVDexivTu1JDnloh7nniPvbe3SNQU_M=> . 


Universal Binary


On the Online Publishers Association blog, the OPA's chief Pam Horan talks online publishing with Edmunds.com CEO Avi Steinlauf. He explains to Horan the benefits of a "Universal Binary" in the mobile space - do you know what it is?.... Steinlauf says, "An iOS Universal Binary simplifies life for mobile users. In our case, users only need to download one app from Edmunds.com and once that happens the site shows up on all their Apple iOS devices. The App is responsive to the platform it runs on, which means that the iPad App has a specific user interface taking advantage of the large screen while on the iPhone and iPod Touch it adapts to a smaller footprint." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001o9GJIHOyP_kRO3jHEQOs_EekdsCNw2G6qt822lv2mryuNVQq-fKT75UUfTDnucvNfRRQMqJVBagfaoPETWxWfOHzJuI3hOC0mIlfTVHHZOwWuCgeB1F8wkcirsMLG9nurLpq23emmAXoQGkkwDUl7tOWwBKCbrufCEQCW8DjnpbiJwCzvbWiAAa9yni9uiww1GqTfTm1X2Jr1nGU3ex3YXgReTl1PMd6km5NjLJHNO1PdZdKFs9AIv3mHMq4Rhci5X_UROygwdo=>

Yahoo! Layoffs


Yahoo! CEO Scott Thompson has begun to cut costs in a big way as The Wall Street Journal reports layoffs yesterday of 2,000 of the company's 14,000 person workforce. Yahoo! sales exec Jim Heckman cites audience buying as his company's salvation. He tells The WSJ, "'A year ago, 'we were facing an impending catastrophe and our revenue was declining, but we've stabilized it and we restored hope,' Now, [Heckman] said, Yahoo can allow advertisers such as auto makers to do 'microscopic audience targeting.'" Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT0XTmGfP6gbZMi71RGwk7zodwX05_Kud_kCtw79jp2iVzfqOfFrfk77zd5InQpSuXHH6XQR--qhCNsNV18UBXgbhpzHdylz4McrkCR0TpubISM6TqYl9BrP2_rLkzECjanYos6E0DxU7lt2af7MbYJqRfscIcG8ns7LNNQ5Apq_Vx9wjp7aJQXX> . And, read Thompson's letter to employees. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT1Ct-hUkTs4xja630bizyYixKHlAJKHcaAtqiIJfwZB6VK-_Y-OHrGjFHW0J1mUe4-E7f1x2w9DnXvfDoZKo8j5tjwncFGA1sORDQiLzYcrxUoq7XzRC3n2_P1UEH8fJIk7Xo-npw1cKEZLYi6ousuJ6laW0aN8bbNbok262phJD-wQ3sClDfwl-htyqQqKmlhb0XYEipnlGw==>  In the coming days, it will be interesting to see how this plays out for Yahoo!'s myriad of ad products and their teams as Yahoo! chooses where to spend, and where to pull back - which will give a better view of the company's strategic direction. 


Give Me Back The UDID


In an effort to find a solution on iOS as Apple's UDID is deprecated, mobile ad companies are coming together for the Open Device Identification Number (ODIN) working group in order to find a solution that addresses privacy concerns while offering effective mobile ad targeting. TechCrunch's Kim Mai-Cutler writes, "ODIN says that about 60 percent of mobile ad revenue comes from this type (UDID) of performance-based advertising. If you factor in cost-per-install or cost-per-action campaigns, which are based on when a consumer downloads an app or takes an action in an app, ODIN says that the app ecosystem could miss out on about $2.6 to $3 million dollars per day in ad revenue." The companies want to find a solution that Apple will accept. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT2_h3pD-c2eZ8HM9hcDEgywPZfAMIqb77vHKki6x9lw8hIy9pxNsiwziVDvwldEEymEWm26c2yu3DFHri6lPaZL1TtYMsSg3P1XlUVB_OMZhvNktrLNRtq4AsI9rPOLyI6mO6eTMNeLcJ4u7Aa2UKFBSQ5kRFtkEIlaQqCpsqvVR15DwTPHHxGMNRSo-TG3xW8rsvn6BxA-eT9E7x2_cz7PVCSfvg-sz6Q=> . And, go to the ODIN mobile site <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT36UtIfcIecwWPc_GpYWDsdm74d2PvB5Q5pr5ru_Sb2-hVYuwy2hx3maPnLWFG2NglplYVOZuYQQ7Xie_yoEQy773bZVpe1a3MADakwfArIboo5QMSNpy7MzsFGr8uufd4=> . ODIN is comprised of Velti, Jumptap, RadiumOne, mdotm, StrikeAd, Smaato, Adfonic and SAY Media. Finally, read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT0cvDs2BLF-1AP8Tk7KYx-LmwahIu1bOsMAeXnbzbm9xWOZcM8j_KPYJIJbpasHk0mCF-2kv4y3tjQDQbt9S-uPVcrBFW8Tges6edcIMd5uZtjlS6nABaI9udwk2J4xUI1w5sx0VU832coPAmSDWuosQZTj17JRo1iGAp6Ub9l40n2IDbQTlj0-yIJlRnhtJsiMHkKWygFHkZbN8VEcBpjiaJNukm0ffVAaQeZ7h59xdNFLzcv-Ir87_U831AlJC5ajCyR1bx76Gg==>  


Audience With Email


A new Exact Target survey helps support the company's core product - email ads. From the release, a "taste" of the findings: "Email -- 96 percent of online consumers use email at least weekly; 66 percent have made a purchase after receiving an email marketing message; 76 percent prefer email over all other channels for customer service messages." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT3EjzL2uC2Sx29Wvkk3qXaL3JEEEWa7Hmg53wO6QRRFUqvLcZcyqbsm54CdzY3q0A3bsjYZhqsjYOSymXs2i6UZ6OjCpMobfJtp1Gc7Ytpqjss_Qpr7JcKZfHUPfF2JWcgDNYpzmuKfm5nVIotnfQW3goAbIMAYLZlA57OYgWHpCmk2ALy5m8KWJnL8fKlSWv5KHy6ePOBP0KB4g1KR96ko-n-zXxenvgjWz3WMR6X0Hg==> . The Business Insider offers the download here (PDF). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT0ezS_qZnGnCjLFCOOJr826AaCXsx2xcDSjHhFuMWjd2XL_HzffSR_tWl5qtRFwuHEnO3-kbeRtcQ6C9hrylCpIPNDdlreUXN9V1KuH66UK2ZznzxQWD0xVbDN3shPXq16-2kJbk6IHtx6EtLbmBn16g9J749OHn9463W5IlkDdqac-hB6eAP0VkDHsZWHq2xh9A4qokP2Gfixa5cAtxa7c>  Deep in the study, the importance of audience targeting remains: "Audience segmentation, data-driven insights, and personally relevant content are no longer 'nice to haves' in email-they are 'MUST haves' for any marketer who wishes to stand out in the inbox." 


Scaling With The COO


Retargeter TellApart is looking to scale its operation as the company announced the appointment of its first-ever Chief Operating Officer. According to a release, new COO Tom Cheli (LinkedIn <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT12WtB_izGWka8-3nKlGYOCYIXThT9nTRe_oOmSr7CCo0ed0RMg_9wIFxLQXB4l0q1LiEHH60Fc9COxhfLnjUz1smkfzocI3ZG6RFPDNszR6fP8LGCnVLVvdkKzYwdm48bQTUMtj3bz4Q==> ) comes from QuinStreet, "one of the largest online direct marketing and media companies in the world, where he was the EVP of Operations." Cheli was a 12-year veteran at QuinStreet where he managed a 700-person operation <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT1edvjPP3-U2CNMUvQWmygILplCiQfrYsuaN1FtDWn-MR3GHRQc42ut30S5bl2gsQjIK73ktAQc4-9Ht74sZkEUphIuo6wWrfNSj7Dq0EKEHlAcFuXP_MsYyXBnulBHH3E=> . Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT3Floy_1T6GhL5RSikHjV38t3jI3Rg2K5kbs9RyOETCcVk3JiAHpXPzZft8m93bW2P3J4I3FTkO_JJ_oe5SCj1fns78mdTZ46mS0lLGvtFkEle5e_9LF_IV_yE6VbLbA0iKogfHsEtIMIIhJxyb0J8-ISdr8L2BC_a97OokSkdrGjTO7RzdmFNtWCmAZDnKUIt9bolgU4cXS0AqPn4h6HIZ> . 


Pre-Bid Data


AdSafe Media pumped up the volume this week as the ad verification firm announced it was bringing "pre-bid," real-time data feeds to demand-side sources. According to the release, "AdSafe's specific ad viewability data points include: The probability of an ad being in view; The probability of the ad scrolling into view; How long the ad will be in view; How long the user will be on the page." Any or all of those are optimization pivot points. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT11KYXjSOrRVQ5vR-Kfiki9IZusjXuBaammwa64OkHEjoq2s29mf-sHhbFgmu6ORz6HwFzfDw_XhIwMjbkcaGPj_0jsF_-YnGXqMyID7ffy0yGdHmutU2wbLVKqtCLIkO94TeRgrDuPOILMQnuxQhphR7rDlHmI2o4vVnvXBvUf6avjjY57YTB98i52s5tWPDglu7CMTLMYT-JD1Fa1VrwxRpWsNpBcFKuRdSt8Ml7X0nG6dQBMfNS0BqJO7necOPDCuALstmdS9g==> . AdSafe also announced a "pre-bid" data deal with search retargeting company Chango but the use case is different: "AdSafe's pre-bid Ad Safety data to score and evaluate the content of individual web pages, ensuring that ads never appear on damaging pages containing adult content, illegal, downloads, offensive language, illegal drugs or hate speech." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT1f0KmGGFEzJvx4zeLqrHQM-vyivbvr7_qvfkhMxnQNo1SIPfIFgAi7Q_JejbMArs7mRKWQwwe4zA2vqb7PUFedfnnyB_VQWGfIS-_yNGRVk4T43d9Qc6Emj2S_FBIrbFb_2alGor_2KOV3_QvzxgqXNdCqiwd-bup-eiic5kRkFbgp0nZzQmZt0JGPpzG8zeHgI2apjdoJKJ17Ia13LoHsoiaZnUVh759aMz46ufIM1CKdc7D99jUA> .

Ad Tech Capitulation


If you didn't make it to ad:tech in San Francisco this week, All Voices' Joseph Thomas brings readers the ad:tech keynote address of LUMA Partners' Terence Kawaja, who sees needed consolidation ahead. Thomas summarizes, "Overall, Kawaja praises the tightening of the fist [around ad tech] because it will ultimately strengthen the industry. He says 2012 is the year of capitulation. Duplicate companies will undoubtedly run out of money and merge with another company to survive." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT0G1xeYtGw9kx7FjZk_tCgngL5Je5FjFyj1krui0n8iqWMfLIQ4n7uK4AAiF9hKxunXzFVZ_IV2pRZQVDpAx3Y9c2gr-KpRKCs1VRFWmqsfvgIPE68uZuU8XoNQOGGCsSPHWIDQrOC7sieg-tFieVVMdvd7gBTtajYktuJqslaGxGDWDyKaWES_M-iQXBPOxwqrYCfG8ki77g==>  And, see the video of the presentation - with slides <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT30FVSA3jAeNbbH8zHqi99lEyDWnHyABgXAOU9JSWFbWXPp4w18xAc9DhWLWlw1l2pfCD0iWBx0GmggdkSQkW5pkcTenRr2R9XDIsss3ByJ7tBOmEzPSqQX6HyEFiS8w5AxWMBU4WfAGz5RuYF7AyWA9-ZHF5a0fqFItjKOIqoOWA==> .


Creative Is Key


A new study by Microsoft Advertising in the UK says that those new IAB Rising Stars units work but.... as Microsoft Advertising's Tim Lumb writes, "Our research found all the campaigns we tested delivered strong increases in attention levels. However not all campaigns successfully transformed the higher attention levels into strong brand uplifts. This tells us that creative execution remains fundamental for driving brand equity." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001lGcyCIEEYT0j5oB6f7NfK_3Ua7gvyJc-31SBEdgXN7MACTdzBUW-IUqQlAUydE5M7HnElp2K8NkfAAeY6OjpShkvXeG83osRlVM9ccqpa-1fNR8RkXrJkJqX1hw2OAGv33RybaEOlXnbnEP2dLa8yo1ySGC5hIwSawnfZWU3vO3kStYJ7Y6ZEeJEi4HAhhD1vzEAwd1mrooC33xoMMK6UkQK3c1b1TfVg9UuFolRz7E1hwK5n4eR-abkCpAQ-QJMV7whOVIB-fo=> . The Search Retargeting Case


Mindshare client ADT says that search retargeting works as DSP Simpli.fi published results of a case study for its search retargeting platform. The release quotes ADT Director of Online Marketing Frank Rivera and claims a 7x improvement in CTR and "ADT achieved a cost per lead (CPL) 95% lower than their benchmark cost per lead." Private Exchanges


OpenX has announced a deal with mobile device manufacturer Samsung to supply the company with a mobile, private ad exchange infrastructure called "the Samsung AdHub Market, Powered by OpenX." It's scheduled to launch in the second-half 2012. The real-time biddable exchange "enables advertisers worldwide to purchase mobile inventory from mobile developers and Samsung Electronics within a closed marketplace environment, allowing easy targeting of desired audiences," according to a release. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8KcMcC_aN6KROr-xsMXuMza9_c2yQbKajkDU7rc--jOJ2kc2xTbpre66_OXUrkAW7xUVVH3MuvPF-PDRzWERSIDk2S5dj6WcEkbYVXmB2d9cn4BZXc-ZrZKe-fR-bCPODbt85zHyjXnItZVg7-d4Yo4b0qqhSTbnwtE-Y9vAWWWlLjB67gfZuOPCtqSWoFwwlyE0HMWlYIRlVOLQAbQ7dKnvKt2QMQZRIUCm3d25Lg8hWQ==>  OpenX CEO Tim Cadogan tells The Wall Street Journal, "'This is the first time any device manufacturer has entered the ad tech space in this way. It is becoming very clear to the principals in the mobile space that advertising is going to be a very important part of the revenue mix.'" If advertisers can use a device's unique identifier and target across devices, that might be especially compelling. Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8KfcdyykzeDN4eqaxJ7ELAFc1uqOu3PfD9v_9NnfX2bCaNznlythGGHZDE9TSR0xu-_Kz-2LmSk-x2Qs-hvoE3hrEqJLtWJWNl4Jur7s4gz_JkWTH6fbuP8_--CJHCtL4wNf2WCeuVugwGFmCAEzv8tjktQJzKWtUXyhzslWi6YS7X3uXDTXdzKs>  Samsung previously made a similar announcement with SmartTV apps in January <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8KcUAWMJyNmJIqPCTC9yUccD7cKuhxDDWUpv1L5YjQa7jtMhO6CuC6HcK1d_cUU6QNanTL5izKSoT665S_Ns9N7dXj1-DohOhQt8rvB2V_5pXNOgORw1-Xc49myMtRjzp4pemVkxcwOlWooWgWMK3o1ggrxdSNWKezOWNdgj387Sv6l_QZ-j_UY--lwtOQPTUZWT68-RjMchUg==> . Google bought Motorola, Singtel bought Amobee <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8Kd68yYBHwREHK0lqKPrD7Kuho98s9zkqRTybUnUHJOZZCbvrtb8RKc1fLxA-54DbvXLV7Kp4GIXzNF8tf8sY08bUygx8hnsX7Sraq9b5zrS7ryDKEiZ7Rf0UH986IhXeW9y0YPbdPo-9cJKQAns4J57kscXIWMoXN032iHubP9_Ag==> , Samsung is getting into the ad business, etc. etc.. Mobile devices love ads and vice versa. 


Do-Not-Track Review


Reuters takes a look online ad targeting in a feature article that reviews privacy regulation and Do-Not-Track's impact both in the U.S. and Europe. Reuters Claire Davenport writes, "You only know these trackers are at work if you read the fine print. The New York Times has a disclaimer saying it hires WebTrends and Audience Science to interpret its readers' interests, and Britain's Guardian newspaper says it pays Criteo and Quantcast, among others, to do the same." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8KcWB6tTm_YQsZ5_BdsgaOVS4zzCcYA_sZCQrzN-hvgTA4ungVBxw_GmiuY7SaqvJ9gSFW12uadF-oYsi52K1TaOtMDeQRB6sTnpZ00qiVT4SV02BZEjPesy522Juz3rNp-XkuDp80UhjiuulVW35LZpMGHksXYvwRcYvclVvc5Z61SxgHYr3TLsraxBOi8HNK4=>  


Going 'Round The Apple


In an Apple UDID <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8KfIRgotHYSfrCAmZJycz4jo6zGgGcvS8AuHdxiqY9ien5TZHJ3VIEWS0aAy4jjDNiB-LLdd2IeaDdKNa_gkSwHnDy4wNxDMbn1u3wMPfzxWnoBlun4DPCvbV4giPMO994seBUhLx8IUJMOIZOvlTerPyVY59bC_k1U=>  end-around, TRUSTe has released a new tool which provides opt-out for mobile tracking for consumers in mobile applications. Or, if the consumer does not opt-out, advertisers can use TRUSTe can to target in-app. MediaPost's Wendy Davis quotes TRUSTe CEO Chris Babel (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8KchMqZPc-p3Cmn6yQhJTVXSJbjoTEUbrpkN8yIqBkEwyCA1hNK-cTHqFVvwTvrONtesjXtAvQmhCf5km_VuBRAyd_xVx0fyFbSO7CoLjw7sCM-7oJfOurFcewSo3QoWnZ5L38dE_xHoQg==> &A 2011) on the new tool, "...Consumers who install the identifier can later effectively delete the data associated with their devices by 'renewing' or 'revoking' it. Consumers who 'renew' the identifier will receive a new one that maintains their opt-out preferences, but isn't tied to their old identifier -- and, therefore, can't be linked to cookie-like data previously associated with their devices." Millennial Media, Jumptap and others have signed on. Don't Quant On It


On ClickZ, Hollis Thomases taps Joanna O'Connell of Forrester Research about what media planners need to know about programmatic buying. O'Connell answers why media planners are having a tough time thusly: "Change is hard and scary. Plus, frankly, planners weren't hired to be technologists or quants. Probably most of them are thinking, 'Why am I not getting to work on the interesting custom brand building stuff?' not, 'Oooh, I love logging into platforms, pulling levers and looking at data.'" This hire also underscores AppNexus' ongoing commitment to building the best leadership team in digital advertising, full stop." This is the second, recent, high-profile hire by AppNexus from the ad network sector as the company hired former Collective sales SVP Andrew Kraft (LinkedIn <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001kvnjnrAU8KfH0MORJtoLjNeD2-vD3NzzYHbVnrpSDjc3lUclzYHDohtYIXhgS-FuZarGyOac_bTxIzqKUg1WKeLb9eNjgvUiqKDhmAJJ4VKoJUhcZca_si17RtvVt42uGCcWmQ456Sc=> ) as its VP of biz dev in February. Rare Crowds


TRAFFIQ's Chief Product Officer Eric Picard has taken the reigns on a new company as TRAFFIQ will segment its digital advertising workflow business led by Lori Goldberg and spin out an emerging opportunity that Picard sees around brand media buying execution at-scale. The new company is called Rare Crowds, as Picard explains, "We're helping media buyers very efficiently make use of ad exchanges and other 'programmatic' inventory sources to buy media for brand advertisers on the basis of targeted reach. This is how almost all dollars are spent offline, and how the majority of dollars are spent on online display. It's about reaching audiences that are a good match for the brand's goals, in an extremely automated way. Our offering is a self-service media buying tool designed for professional media buyers, and is a very complementary offering to DSPs and the trading desk practices within the holding companies..." See the site <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6vG8FKeaW-4NVJ2_qmsrAf-_tM-TwKkO4RMQFNjy3BzQJBw4IoWaikeQG4rATWcAZDLd7rBZS5-Qa5goGuUKSFa5V7pED7oE4CkawmbR1HPrQ==> . 


Real-Time Streaming


Dr. Robert Plant (no, not that Robert Plant <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6s-83sSzrWlbDCZA3y-wPpGYrceHd9TU1GwHS0h4sx4btiHp6q4sxhGX0_-F8j0MtODrzftB_1O_cA1Rdjitbs1OqcTQm0_7oP4SdIdsGGjK2IAqSOHkSq0T_vVhhpVspv33j0VUxcKgQ==> ) from the University of Miami trumpets the beneficial uses of data in real-time in an op-ed of sorts in the Wall Street Journal. Dr. Plant notes the origins of real-time data's benefits - streaming stock quotes, "Streaming already has transformed the financial-services industry. It is hard to imagine that investors once made trading decisions based on price data that was delayed 20 minutes. But streaming is starting to reshape, or has the potential to reshape, a host of other industries, as well. Here's a closer look." Read examples (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6sQy-2v8z_0dt4a912Ftp6w3LIqFBuJD8cZT2J1YClnGqp3S0BewNKgbgwl7DMSYfPz63z7e0_h8QTPiZ3Rc4j0TsoXCzi2xU3mn7pR-VZheFHPsFTu9ABZTqdxWbmfhexcJuoaUrHIdyy4duMeCPigOmoVzWS5n06aUJQYLeWdheyxPb4vRAXB>  - however obtuse, nearly all have implications for ads. 


Leaving The Trough


Venture capital guy Doug Pepper provides a graphic or two on tech products that hit the hype cycle, then fall into a trough and, finally, power up toward "sustainability." Pepper writes, "For entrepreneurs and investors the most exciting element of the Market Curve is that, once the trough ends, strong technology markets ultimately prove more valuable than anyone imagined even during the Hype Cycle." Where do the DSP/SSP/Exchange models fall? From here, they're coming out of the trough. Not a bad trough, either. Read about the lifecycle of tech markets. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6suN30LLk0Md_RJk2JIRNMIn_4N1R4c6FJPTXNbYTg4P9YmV0BeNvRMAVEaRVEjHgHdtkT24zItzeBXit_UpiLIOcP8FPYQlmMWDhmGT4dYS4iOYiLDTlqpT-ym7CMgYxgcNYgDkWYAhWXmXn6-EuGjqhSr-E0rRGyjz9OEgDqPmQ==>  


Gamifying The Skip


Following the footsteps of Publicis VivaKi's The Pool <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6u836MwPu32jCSdQZU0pVirSYHxKHg-rlCo6lb86-HpIbTxIjeKYpKhsLy-3pH6_Rdj6tkaJKlgbn8oxUvQEYAaeve93O3kXhcVCxd4Dds2TP9J3kDHjMIN>  initiative, Google <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6v4UMStpB_q8_k9on17jfq5ousMKFamDYmLl5cjUmRoASvrdbghsW2TeGueqAPaCkYT6L9N7bcdDG4eB6cslXZ0gTDEVopQFhffkCUabGWZYXB1PG9SOFn076hKK09HxtHtaYR5mgRCUqQ8RLYNQHQDZsIsAsibNSPmnrIaE8TpXpCDX2i75colWuvm_RWfQp4=>  and Solve Media <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6vnLxfqO9cJpsLE-1V6qlawQ_-xeXYiIwiwTUhtk5BMkafEwndvKFyTI515WkkdfQMLKe4W0jIHTampnZHwAnYYk2E3XR9wLCyQkgIq6uRqsVe2nGqYgR935iPpzkdpgVGLuqRvh7rDl1FftKpQMR2ypqdxK0DxtjnfVBQIpg96nleydJFBS-3BnjxlVJNCCSjhDP8HvEoL6c13SQSmUEHzAxG5U1hPTbLyHXKLAkWYg8U_gew2L5V6tO5tIuzSNqFtxNAVutS_9JhbqZrfPwdwzvcfgbnzYP0=>  among others, video ad network and exchange SpotXchange is bringing its own brand of skippable video ads. Called "Skip It" - SpotXchange "takes the cake" with the most intuitive brand name and and adds a gaming element that requires user sign up to skip ads. The SkipIt blog <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6tXM0EBztIUneJ1N0722WbvkXInJoLqSRGSpkGqplvNN3bSvOqDM7wpPfbbQLSqvZ0MabjTgIl6Rr1MojSwY1nRVi-CxPQU0pw5FK_-hbv0e720jIBC4AgS1THFMswOaErU6FRcV4jhzywzy8dUgRA3yOIPFKAB5zc=>  explains, "...you can earn tons of free skips. For each friend you refer that also signs up and funds their account with $10, you earn another 5 free skips. Plus, for every dollar you put in your SkipIt account, you earn 1 free skip. So $10 = 10 free skips. Then you can start skipping video ads to your heart's content." Visit the publisher sign-up - publisher.skipit.com <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6u2o-KaaPilF3C7FXjK2S1lNQoJKsMHzEUqUHYu8QpZuiKUFHiBXcLrfXOEcBf3LcYfsSn1xs-Fbw4wucH038FfEmkQnP3Z9MGioac2I8MiYQ==> . 


My Name's ROI - Capital R-O-I


Hey analytics lovers, the Nielsen Wire blog offers thoughts from a recent marketing effectiveness whitepaper on what metrics brand marketers should consider when determining ROI. Once such metric: "Price Premium: 21 percent of advertised brands in our study did not command a price premium over their nearest non-advertised competitor. This could possibly be a result of excessive promotions, ineffective advertising messages, inadequate product features, etc." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6tUu5WAHcSriuCIJWwAwelkYkdVsDFkwzHhYM__uIaEMRSTaLmWDM8KfDoK6EgxqLY7ms11gT19akpceeRD4ufzB4bAc0g32kt_ashppHZzzEy8Ghs_dRcbRlcaX5Xu9IQGcJO4V7AviI-am1qEcA-wEdvpIa_YmTfMZnmxAFmkuSfRtoFLQjyQec6ii3YyxcmmNDhhStQeGJHNqiq_5thG> . And, download the study (sign-up required) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6vmdSPf6-Y0E7h29pZxl8eZQgegGshjv6aCwh4lC63APWklpYNkvGKiVa5aj3tOS2vzTN2HEqsVvLpCuLLqVPJytBiOKaPqCMxb6rnrIBBBoTaxihOtOhCjvjDfKMUn6lS35X3i3XCPHCIUo-zfjP3JlK0cTWOTvpaKkqsGbhctz_uyOoZmXUcr7GW2l5xDGLEGX0suPRSV9A==> .

The Privacy Icon


ClickZ's Kate Kaye reports that just as the Digital Advertising Alliance's Managing Director, Peter Kosmala, has left his position to take a new role at the 4As (LinkedIn <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6v7143JZvYeP11E61aztoGVqTo2Xi0z5rruOcjVHWrzoa_YDHpSdebcJbVTIh45gqUyj8cj71tgxuZRNb5sklMJ21OlIR76fxIdOlKiI3lP83JGtHhkFyZ8k4MR2RzN79E-WuA4Muc0pA==> ), the privacy icon which the DAA oversees is under scrutiny. Kaye writes, "Research published today from Carnegie Mellon University suggests the DAA's AdChoices icon was not recognizable to web users when a study was conducted last year. In its small 'Smart, Useful, Scary, Creepy: Perceptions of Online Behavioral Advertising' study conducted in August 2011, Carnegie Mellon found that around half of users surveyed - 25 of 48 - had never seen the ad icon when showed it in context." Either 23 of the 48 users need to subscribe to the AdExchanger newsletter <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6tNdwvFdUYQsEcEXjXD6dHZYHeo4z6IaDQCcVznfMgR8_T7GP7iayXQgqfs2qabnvmUCM_Nvcqrl6_ETXZSQN4ReIN3qBbvpGvuajsAYfiGDQyQv8uPKsZUzDlT2NyC9iE=> , or the DAA and its supporting bodies need to continue raising awareness. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6tVK4QC8Xf4uGsb1qzA8Bnp-RBGasDnQui8Jw2Si9Z62q0z-fF2tHl-_nWymFv_oVEALm2mMlGD6da4CNM2KMhd0HQn1P1InWNr4oPFgurtoq0CXCLra0LbXUg4S89dp2Tq1IcxErbj75ucIqARKLhP6vww03qLLFYihr3ZT3n1xtuQsgPhWzoaFJwACrjupXo=>  And, download the study (PDF). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6t6GFOXEwktmLlr6OvGUM4lf8RMrq9q4O5ETbh_IMmduhqoFsaNZjJDLP4h7cMqxjJoXFXPyemmDrB-5VHk5qcTZzuO1GyB6EtQTNjm9VPpMUkgZMG5ohrZ4btb8EZ8ZA1SlijkfvbtwVq37ERKnYm0c44doxB7jFwCR6p5RkJ1gw==>  


Give Me Data


B2B data company Bizo, a 2008 ZoomInfo spinoff <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6sQgGMp0alaGexn7H5IAxTROxLhCn6iEMs9_MTAVVnzP5_CmLgaHPGtK9Bwzacn-JFZ_lPBCwKXArUxUVXcs66PFQ0wx-KvMZqX-4W2_xUFUq8oPpUpLrq6DMvaxw3MoaD2PV6Qlur4maOJf5OcS2yyFu45cgDQdE0B9PaCZZWaW_Wy9GDlEf4LHlF30tI-hEX85TiFpUOLc0iQMZDrJ0c_> , has recorded its second or third round of funding - depending on how you're counting (Crunchbase <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6vVWyU3jiJWV0gPsrJhV3rM-hkYQw6PES_R1J1MzYMtEoQOzrY5mjcGPQWoqA8KOeW2SAB4aOr2L1TI3fORr4wmVsyH0txIReQmoilf5l71YxjNlhD3ZuvwWD2QokUba38=> ) - inclusive of a new $10 million round led by Crosslink Capital. Interesting to see a targeting-data-centric company receive investment after a lull in that sector of the funding marketplace (eXelate, BlueKai last raised in 2010; DataLogix in 2009, for example). Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eGWccCAUY6seuBtJyLZUlXVl6WA1z6D4ewmV_Sbok92H9WHjoln8m0juJAdXFByg_9JBZ53YZP9h0cmoie9RYYXiNcePdOrvxbSxO3LWZOjAG1HuTYNjNEWGBjtiF4CjLMVuFxHNK8wnzBzon1iRIqLOgr05OthZZ-GI098_6SFO1xJ0tbRoJao6nHyxX_U1OIqDzcPW-MZ4gczWn6OOPR6w8DC5mbpz16m31E_o6fn9C89KQE3zimsuvPLOXllh> .

iAd Amps Rev Share


Apple is raising its revenue share for developers on the iAd mobile ad network. Apple Insider notes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKS9geStVSzgrPTj2JVVIQKDfXuAYKWJJnh6V5n1185lkgjTNVIi3dN_Fr7SYRnlWJrrWpLUVLpuGUO2IWsKRM-nXE1D4iXF0wKgwTEYqBZy_7IpOGXRlingspmepPZuFCVXT1lyBjRwQV6Yq_KkepSRYjgzwg1SqKA9Dwmsy_YIs_L3Xvfm_mt2ilLgN3Unyb70hyXUqXGwINQzN5vsza0J>  that the increase is an improvement of 10% for developers - now 70%. Considering the cash hordes of Apple, it will be interesting to see how Google responds with AdMob and its mobile ad network efforts in-app and on the mobile web. Read Greg Sterling's take on MarketingLand. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKSawgqqxba7q-3FBm7KQx7nxxW7ZpeZ4M8xolS_SgEo2DtWgTdQ-DttmG_ivT9t98rqWzV-fmexvoQh46evBjFrVKG_YbqcKzqPlmL5Zweg38u7scMf1VLj_Ol7NPsISFM2TJ0CMuEMUtLYmOk_0FbEGLSV_bd8RaATPs7S6p_X5WL28eN9xvgqOzt5PnEV7qtdEaPha7Lfuw==>  It would seem possible that rev shares will continue tilting even more in the favor of developers as Google and Apple battle it out to win the mobile ads race by fueling incentives. Is 100% to developers far off? Visit Apple's developer blog <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKQUeqTuop6QtEnumMzbt7ErdM5mM88Ypih1OkaQzlbLV6YkgkoPXFKYyvzHSpuU7-ul1USuoj7oVOEy_KBWQkjKt5RQv9QlaO0QbQ3e1k_OBaEuWJFVV65bA7osXppKuFwOpvYKul-Db08FBnmsAkTN> . To date, iAd has struggled with its positioning as well-publicized rate cuts for advertisers hurt the brand's mojo. 


MRAID For MROBILE


Mobile rich media provider Mixpo is looking to make noise by following the IAB's MRAID (Mobile Rich Media Ad Interface Definitions) spec <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKRA4OvF4DwI8MgayAxb00ZemSI-Ocn_5tlnxesm49So4_D9rKMv9K0b2HbGFRJ8m-zyaCkxEalYR1Uw_qo7DmxqiHEGb0mUlEU7oMg7WjJquA==>  which standardizes "mobile rich media ads that will run in mobile apps." Mixpo says it has partnered with video monetization platform Freewheel to expand its reach. FreeWheel VP of biz dev Brent Horowitz says in the press release, "Partnering with Mixpo for in-app advertising gives our global media customers the flexibility to monetize their video with more rich, personalized, and compelling interactive video ad experiences." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKRz6DwWZJA3mZ_uVMx6-eD77EKqa8qM_kUfMJJhXm1aezdGq_r_oFQ9xsF-Ha9f0JcnEiMUELww0gHQCqCelbBVGRL7ovp0duhIHgketqtwvi3Jq3CC6S06JTON8hFTdXjRyYqxPLaTPZ_MqW7Jxn7UYAXN0N7Q0huFfNTA4aOyRBaz0sO-OjI-AWMrZwZlk1x2JJNe5N4whskRrW9lCRuOio0ZaeRx7yQXO_Q08eR771LZcFQ8iPEzV2EN5azYYiE=> . Ahh, the push and pull of standardization. From here, it seems some ad tech companies don't want it -whether it's MRAID, VAST or some other acronym. For example, if an video ad network/tech vendor can create a network of publishers with reach and scale that uses a proprietary format - that's barrier-to-entry! Ch-ching. Closed makes money until the open world catches up - or closed becomes the new open. Ironically, little guys and big guys want to undo these proprietary networks as both see them as a threat. Hence, standardization efforts.


Amazon Forking Google


From the Flurry blog, the quiet media giant, Amazon, is said to be outperforming Google when it comes to mobile apps. Flurry head of marketing Peter Farago - a maestro of link bait - writes, "Amazon's bet to fork Android in order to put consumers into their own shopping experience on Kindle Fire appears to be paying off. Showing its commerce strength, Amazon already delivers more than three times the revenue in its app store compared to what Google generates for developers." Fork it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKQGAGLJMNvrvy8Lg6Znje5a4lGpeuoZjN7TuvVQO6x42__IS6yHjSec2utwzsfSVydJ4HakK4Fi8sNJzJ2tf6qpZJS4ojhG2qHoz-VlUl62-ZfFyRsYQgqg66DOqsiizyBABTL9bXwbcnLUT4sgkBcYXRcWSVLbVdFtlu6t9iGgbBxLMshtCPczhfxhBWTaSZ9EkPFu5kG-sA==>  


First-Party DMP


AT&T AdWorks said late last week that it has partnered with DMP/DSP Turn for an audience management platform. According to a Turn release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKQvKZv4CinqT-bNTecWdFe77eznnAGGZEW_y8dJ-S-ykJpcl6lGjtRGVaoto6gXXs-cxf16zPMY89oxMiJ-UJ8M6Xm_zdhpdYZwjtnUkWBth7CwOa7erXKn9bMj-xxIqyKjc_XFlGeucgZLVFXtAdm0TcogBpUiRqChoEiQCBK3vUsI2CSNGHxYZ9SaKLyOFPxgFC-J6RPsAMfoAUT3pP39HqAk2AwhZho=> , "The jointly developed platform stores anonymous AT&T data within a private cloud, which protects consumer privacy by encrypting all data that leaves the private cloud." Turn CEO Bill Demas tells AdExchanger that's what's different about this private cloud solution is that it stores only ATT data: "Think of it as hermetically sealed. In this case we encrypt even the descriptors for the data and this is held safely behind the ATT firewall. No one other than ATT has access to the data and no one else can decrypt the data." Turn is getting deeper into the first-party data business. Hello Acxiom, Experian, etal.? Acxiom CEO Scott Howe used to be (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKSQE1YRaCS8F9ox07GCEx2jSY6L5UQDzHl2_7RhXQiuOh16Cww_uNeDtkrRbQwa_0-1NQhm7Q1SQ46hK2O3ULUIYgUG05GimDjcWTBRrwVozCsAhQdZ_PvZ2tfaItDjj8BVydkEiY43d0P15-kp2Kgs> &A) on Turn's board <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKTSouclqMzqTIIaQl_UaJDP5XSiwqqv9CfMlhQHts0R3ZzSOHZXAAz1WlSqUPlrfg7bm5OBXQMzDiiSS8Sg-88UsKvHifrz8-Z7aJq_1ZlSKg==> .. the plot thickens. 


R-M-X-I-N-I


Neustar, owners of TARGUSinfo, is taking part of its R&D to the University of Illinois campus (I-L-L, I-N-I) and fund the Neustar Innovation Center which the press release says will explore and address a range of "big data" issues including fraud prevention and large scale networking. Leading the division will be a former Yahoo!, Ken Taylor (LinkedIn <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKQ3lktZmZF9vV9nQVBYBSNimx_goFe6N2isLldT2n8bof3HGTC5tr3agh8a-aohbhyc7CWNfxNtwpGsZuvqrvrNkAmBF2Yr2lkVtQ0XI7V_LJS2eCDrM2isCT3eJsh65f0=> ), who will "serve as the director of the Neustar Innovation Center. Prior to joining Neustar, Taylor served as technology principal for Yahoo! Right Media Exchange where he focused on large-scale data processing, collection and analysis." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKQMd1hKLaVMXcmpmpsd6wOJCz551NWsEG09oFhW8URVnbmUaxctIoPTMKkJ5yWCA4-TnVnroJrtC89_OaBOmCtODStes24J9VCJOPGv5g8W9nKyB3b2eWBIWFd44Ukz6XI5w8KqgKPuGcuPPgcyxw9EF78RipKYGDYYo4P2Dhm6OIT86kLLev2Dh5B3SeQ6NHrfzywzR7lSnLgSeyAyMXNhmdfj98LOzDV-Mh6KN8LNHRq55k3ePEFnLP8m5aZwqoL2lDZPccYICz0CJzj0jrCDS6R55XWPi73qQmqiopmy7BN4abSGH7uxZDbZtH0iMEqZ2gxp3QO7YqRqvjDPv0gMgiwjA0YVuy2C6RGFGBWp2w==> . This isn't the first time a public or private company has funded research at a university, but considering the constraints around hiring and the growing cash at certain media tech companies, this sort of deal may make increasing sense. 


Facebook Ads, India, Exchanges


In TechCircle.in, Nandana Das claims there is a battle brewing in India between Ozone Media, which has a inked a deal to sell various types of ad placements on Facebook, and Komli Media. Komli's India managing director Gulshan Verma says his company has an exclusive deal to sell "premium" placements in India - and that Ozone sells the same Facebook media everyone else does in India. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKTJn-5cBfgkm2MUzv8M6lZZw0ZdY2LcUjdzC-dbHZOZqyeBqzP2ibeFWOzthYJRmpPUwFPntoY_fqmeNagvLNnjikN39QKMT92gvOuyhy78NDUr9GGUewZyjiFmTdu0RJi9W1UUOc-coEeFwLDuuKI7r_Np-vfIw1szxrzDsROXjBvgDwbUflQjxVN1PTqMd5Y=> . Verma tells TechCircle.in, "From time to time, Facebook does make available some inventory on Google Ad Exchange, which only large-volume bidders on the exchange have access to." 


Measuring Transactions


Boutique investment bank Petsky Prunier takes its turn tallying the mergers and acquisitions data for the first quarter of 2011. The company says that in the marketing, media, tech and service industries transaction value was up 44% compared to Q4 2011. Also on a quarter-over-quarter basis, transaction volume was down 6%. Also of note - Groupon had the most strategic transactions in the quarter at 5. View the release (PDF). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKTTeTEve2JK4C8t7yPUZVCl8C009DVu7UCO6GmqkaPkeUK-881oUO3DZG7ZKpBbi7XaxsK6qX8vu0cPVq0VTrZ7lxGB1cU1txlCrVTFVoeI4LNvf2kQs5ljjB-slEY7PzZKGMMeJK3Ksc8GLee-BGY8xNhhnJKhpFG3TGeh7Mrki39TGJDPPkW2>  Facebook will surely be in this ballpark once the IPO hits. 


European Gloom?


"Online retail sales grew 18% in Europe in 2011, even as the region struggled with a financial crisis," begins Mark Brohan of Internet Retailer as he covers new data from UK-based The Centre for Retail Research. Anecdotal evidence points to success across Europe in e-Commerce in spite of economic tribulations. For example, Brohan writes, "In Germany, Otto Group, No. 2 in the Top 400 Europe, used a mix of new business development and better customer service to grow its e-commerce revenue 26.3% in its 2011 fiscal year to 4.8 billion euros ($6.2 billion)." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?et=1109658719196&s=8442&e=001catxkZl1RKSC__JdubqJjdvTyKGPC3a-fKxrg0dCA8VEr9bID3XzPDy7Ktybumz8oHUuKbRk7sZBdauQeXPt1fJddgqXlYSKqzthssyI_aK6ycYhvMlaplfmXZgyZ6RdTNUTJA3FzasZYO-RcJPLv7EoNdJVC8ncX4KULmUJAmp6bZN45lk5Ga5jS6kzbMVo> . More e-Commerce means more European, display ad retargeting opportunities.
